        <p class="date">
         Mon Jun 09, 2014 at 06:44 PM PDT
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/06/10/1305673/-Lt-Col-Robert-Bateman-challenges-the-NRA" id="titleHref">
          Lt. Col. Robert Bateman challenges the NRA
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Demi Moaned">
          Demi Moaned
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=101809&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/06/10/1305673/-Lt-Col-Robert-Bateman-challenges-the-NRA" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="Lt. Col. Robert Bateman challenges the NRA" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/06/10/1305673/-Lt-Col-Robert-Bateman-challenges-the-NRA" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="164" data-story_id="1305673" href="/story/2014/06/10/1305673/-Lt-Col-Robert-Bateman-challenges-the-NRA#comments">
           164 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          It's been some time now since I added Charles Pierce's
          <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/">
           'The Politics Blog' over at
           <em>
            Esquire
           </em>
          </a>
          to my daily blogroll. His righteous indignation coupled with his madcap prose stylings are
          <em>
           sui generis
          </em>
          and often hilarious. But, although Pierce is the proprietor and primary contributor to the blog, other writers are sometimes featured. Among them is a semi-regular whom I've come to increasingly appreciate named
          <strong>
           Lt. Col. Robert Bateman
          </strong>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          Bateman is active-duty Army, 'an infantryman and a Military Fellow at the Center for Strategic and International Studies (CSIS)' and currently stationed in England. His primary recurring feature at 'The Politics Blog' is the
          <a href="http://www.esquire.com/archives/blogs/politics/by_tag/Esquire%20Civil%20War%20Reenactment/15;1">
           Civil War Reenactment
          </a>
          an as-it-happened 150 years ago today recounting of the military events of the Civil War. But he's not one of those sentimentalists who appreciate the beauty and valor of the South's struggle. He unapologetically refers to it as
          <strong>
           The War of Southern Rebellion
          </strong>
          and considers Robert E. Lee a traitor. The
          <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/civil-war-grant-lee-end-of-line-060314">
           last installment in the series to date
          </a>
          had Grant stalemated just a few miles from Richmond.
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          But he also writes on other topics. He has been strong in his denunciation of sexual assault and rape in the military, as in
          <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/navy-court-martial-results-rape-051614">
           this recent post
          </a>
          . And he has been increasingly critical of our country's gun culture.
         </p>
         <p>
          In
          <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/chipotle-bans-guns-from-restaurants-052114">
           this post from May 21
          </a>
          , he championed the group
          <strong>
           Mothers Demand Action Against Gun Violence
          </strong>
          for their successful confrontation of Open Carry Texas over guns at Chipotle:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "Open Carry Texas" (which I think of as "Wimps With Mommy Issues"), conducted an open carry, en masse, at a Chipotle Restaurant  then the moms shared the word. They posted pictures of these morons carrying rifles in a family restaurant. Then they asked that the chain bar weapons on their private property. As Founder Shannon Watts put it: "The Chipotle petition received more than 10,000 signatures within just a few hours." The corporation realized where their business interests lie and that guns are wrong in their establishments across the entire nation.
          <br/>
          ...
          <br/>
          These women are doing what nobody else had managed to do before now. They are actually affecting change. Not through legislation, but through the free choice they have to patronize, or to NOT patronize, private companies that allow guns to be carried in their stores, restaurants, malls, and more.
         </blockquote>
         I thought that was pretty bold. But there's even stronger stuff in today's post, headlined:
         <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/i-am-coming-home">
          'That's It. I Am Coming Home."
         </a>
         .
         <blockquote>
          <strong>
           This is too much
          </strong>
          . We have Tea Party political activists shooting cops from behind, in the head, then covering their dead bodies with the Tea Party Gadsden flag and shouting, The Revolution begins now!
          <p>
           No. I am coming home. I need to be there and be part of the solution.
           <a href="http://www.momsdemandaction.org/">
            Moms Demand Action
           </a>
           is getting some traction, but they can use the lean-in of a few U.S. Army Airborne Infantry Rangers. I am only sorry that I did not stand up to this threat to our nation before. I am sorry. I was busy.
          </p>
          <p>
           I have been overseas in Afghanistan and in NATO nations for half a decade while the insanity of the National Rifle Association expanded and exploded, and the NRA became, essentially, the tool of death in the United States. They made mass killings normal.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         It's pretty much an open declaration of war on the NRA. He is a brave man. He has already received a lot of hate mail. So, he seems to have no illusions about the risks. But he openly taunts them:
         <blockquote>
          Wimps need guns. Come and get me.
          <p>
           Oh, and if you try to go lethal, to convince me that your rhetoric is more intellectually compelling than my own written words, I am going to be giggling at the Las Vegas odds on you, with your guns, and me.
          </p>
          <p>
           So there is that. Bring it on, little boys.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         Anyway, I am very proud of him and I wanted to bring him to your attention because he deserves our support and encouragement.
        </div>
       </div>
       <h4>
        Originally posted to
        <a href="/blog/Demi Moaned/">
         Demi Moaned
        </a>
        on Mon Jun 09, 2014 at 06:44 PM PDT.
       </h4>
       <h4>
        Also republished by
        <a href="/blog/Shut Down the NRA and Amend the Second Amendment/">

        </a>
        and
        <a href="/blog/Repeal the Second Amendment RSA/">
         Repeal or Amend the Second Amendment (RASA)
        </a>
        .
       </h4>

        <div>
         <p>
          Add keywords that describe this diary.
		Separate multiple keywords with commas.
          <br/>
          <a href="/special/tag_tips" target="_blank">
           Tagging tips
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/search?search_tags=1" target="_blank">
           Search For Tags
          </a>
          -
          <a href="http://www.dkosopedia.com/wiki/Tag:Tagfinder" target="_blank">
           Browse For Tags
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="pageTip hasTooltip" style="margin-top:3px">
          ?
         </div>
         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>

           <li id="c162">
            <div class="cx" id="cx53655579">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               When I could still sing- I sang the Messiah or
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1305673/53655579#c162?mode=alone;showrate=1#c162">
                0+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               parts of it dozens and dozens of time often several times each season. And sang in volunteer caroling groups to raise money for civic choruses.
              </p>
              <p>
               I always tried to convince the carolers to do the "All We Like Sheep", like sheep, Bah, Bah etc.
              </p>
              <p>
               The music is light and frivolous. I think the showman, Handel, and he was a showman, would approve.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:135801">
                Marnie1
               </a>
               on
               <a href="/comments/1305673/53655579#c162">
                Wed Jun 11, 2014 at 05:01:30 PM PDT
               </a>
              </p>
              <p class="cl">

               I know a former Special Forces colonel
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1305673/53646031#c145?mode=alone;showrate=1#c145">
                5+ / 0-

                </a>
                ,
                <a href="/user/uid:1000367">
                 raspberryberet
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               Used to teach ROTC at UMass, had been a LRRP in 'Nam. He was definitely the sort who could (and probably had) killed with his toenail clippings -
              </p>
              <p>
               And no, he didn't talk about combat. Ever. He'd talk about jokes he played on people, he'd talk about the whorehouse he and a couple of buddies co-owned in Saigon, he'd talk about going to Harvard after he was discharged, he'd talk about how he hated
               <i>
                Platoon
               </i>
               not only for the ridiculous plot but because the mud was the wrong color.
              </p>
              <p>
               He'd talk about anything military...except for combat. He'd seen too much and done too much to share it.
              </p>
             </div>

         <ul class="cm i1" id="k53635076">
          <li id="c127">
           <div class="cx" id="cx53641615">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              My Vietnam experience
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1305673/53641615#c127?mode=alone;showrate=1#c127">
               5+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:998110">
                Rita5018
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:1029751">
                jbwoman
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:1027543">
                Silencio
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:976721">
                bearsguy
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:37492">
                Wayward Wind
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              When Nixon had US forces illegally invade the sovereign nation of Cambodia I felt that my job as an infantry medic (Corpsman) was somehow wrong. I walked to the company commander and told him that I could no longer support our efforts in Vietnam. I was very upset but I let him convince me to return to my unit and my job as Corpsman. Sometimes I regret not standing by my convictions even though it would have meant jail.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
             </p>
             <p class="cb">
              by
              <a href="/user/uid:979391">
               JimValent
              </a>
              on
              <a href="/comments/1305673/53641615#c127">
               Tue Jun 10, 2014 at 01:53:15 PM PDT
              </a>
             </p>
             <p class="cl">
              [
              <a href="#c17">
               Parent
              </a>
              ]
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
          </li>
          <ul class="cm i1" id="k53641615">
           <li id="c139">
            <div class="cx" id="cx53645157">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               Medics
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1305673/53645157#c139?mode=alone;showrate=1#c139">
                2+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:330318">
                 JerryNA
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="/user/uid:976721">
                 bearsguy
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               were by far the bravest - or perhaps craziest - people I met in Vietnam and Cambodia, and I owe my life to a couple of them.
              </p>
              <p>
               Tonight I will raise a glass of Glenfiddich to you....
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
               I am a warrior for peace. And not a gentle man... Steve Mason, 1940-2005
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:37492">

            <li id="c151">
             <div class="cx" id="cx53649705">
              <h5>
               <a class="de">
               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                I think corpsmen (medics) are the highest number
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1305673/53649705#c151?mode=alone;showrate=1#c151">
                 1+ / 0-
                </a>
                )
               </span>
              </h5>
              <div class="crs">
               <dl>
                <dt>
                 Recommended by:
                </dt>
                <dd>
                 <a href="/user/uid:37492">
                  Wayward Wind
                 </a>
                </dd>
               </dl>
              </div>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                of Congressional Medal of Honor recipients, many awarded posthumously. I was not a corpsman, but I am proud to have served with them.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="cf">
               <p class="sig">
               </p>
               <p class="cb">
                by
                <a href="/user/uid:330318">
                 JerryNA
                </a>
                on
                <a href="/comments/1305673/53649705#c151">
                 Wed Jun 11, 2014 at 07:42:36 AM PDT
                </a>
               </p>
               <p class="cl">
                [
                <a href="#c139">
                 Parent
                </a>
                ]
               </p>
              </div>
             </div>
            </li>
            <ul class="cm i1" id="k53649705">
             <li id="c152">
              <div class="cx" id="cx53650033">
               <h5>
                <a class="de">
                </a>
                <span class="cu">
                 I have a good friend, Gary Beikirch,
                </span>
                <span class="crd ntb">
                 (
                 <a href="/comments/1305673/53650033#c152?mode=alone;showrate=1#c152">
                  2+ / 0-
                 </a>
                 )
                </span>
               </h5>
               <div class="crs">
                <dl>
                 <dt>
                  Recommended by:
                 </dt>
                 <dd>
                  <a href="/user/uid:1000367">
                   raspberryberet
                  </a>
                  ,
                  <a href="/user/uid:976721">
                   bearsguy
                  </a>
                 </dd>
                </dl>
               </div>
               <div class="ct">
                <p>
                 who was a SF medic who was awarded the Medal of Honor, and his story is incredible. After the Army, he moved into the mountains of New Hampshire, lived in a cabin he built himself, and by the time they tracked him down to notify him of the award, his hair was down to his waist. Heh...
                </p>
                <p>
                 The medics that I served with were just amazing - one quiet and reserved, one quirky as hell and what kids today would call a dork, one brash and full of jokes and pranks. But when the SHTF, they were there, never hesitating.
                </p>
                <p>
                 I was wounded twice, the second time very seriously, and I would not be here typing this if it were not for them.
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="cf">
                <p class="sig">
                 I am a warrior for peace. And not a gentle man... Steve Mason, 1940-2005
                </p>
                <p class="cb">
                 by
                 <a href="/user/uid:37492">
                  Wayward Wind
                 </a>
                 on
                 <a href="/comments/1305673/53650033#c152">

                 </a>
                </p>
                <p class="cl">

            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Real men who have actually been in real combat
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1305673/53648266#c149?mode=alone;showrate=1#c149">

            <p>
             are more interested in safety and do not believe that, as the man who avoided his generation's war because of a nervous disorder, states, "The only thing that will stop a bad man with a gun is a good man with a gun". It seems Wayne LaPierre, the good man with a gun was exempt fropm fighting all those bad guys with guns in Nam. I believe Wayne's affliction may cause me to have a nervous disorder because of his leadership of a gun group. Too bad Wayne was not in a leadership role of the NRA in my generation's war, then I could have claimed a nervous disorder (if there was such a thing back then) and been exempted from serving.
            </p>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               more than a few times. But I've a lot of years under my belt, too. We own a gun and do occasionally use it on our property, ~26 acres of deep southern Appalachian forest surrounded by National Forest and state game lands. We've all sorts of reasons for a gun here. And sometimes we just shoot because it's time to do some refresh and clean 'em out.
              </p>
              <p>
               All my neighbors are more armed than I am, and then there's the wayward hunters who can't read a Posted sign. It's always some kind of season here, it seems.
              </p>
              <p>
               Do know my way in and around. So do my kids and grandkids (in their 20s). Deal is, I'm not afraid of the looks of a gun. You bring one into a public establishment where I'm with my loved ones, and I am flat outta there from the nearest - hopefully alarmed - emergency outlet. I don't carry in public, I sure as hell don't expect to meet it in public. If I do, I am fully prepared to get between it and my loved ones, and try to talk 'em down. Simply not being afraid goes a long way in the 'sane' armed world. Honest.
              </p>
              <p>
               That's why freaking cowards like this shoot people in the back. This is entirely unacceptable in a civilized society.

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               to own a gun ought to be enough in control of their own minds not to fall for a hack job sales spiel. Fear is the motivator for both the wacko gunnies AND the terrorized public. Fearful people don't tend to live peaceful lives, but continually seek out ways to 'conquer' their fear. Guns are definitely the wrong way to conquer fears.

               I've never carried a gun openly or concealed in a public place. I've never once felt I needed to, and most certainly never
               <b>

              </p>
              <p>
               Too much fear, anger and hate in a society where too many people can't see a future because they've been collectively robbed of all hope for a future. The solution just isn't that difficult - institute the Catch-22. If you are so frightened and paranoid and angry and hateful that you feel the need to brandish guns in public, then you're too mentally unstable to be allowed a gun to brandish.
              </p>
              <p>
               Yoda was right, you know...

               Fear leads to anger.

               Hate leads to suffering.

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I have been reading Pearce for a while now and regularly add comments to what has been written.
           </p>
           <p>
            Pearce, Stewart, and Colbert provide all the information you need to know that you don't miss anything if you don't watch the Sabbath Gasbags.
           </p>
           <p>
            Bateman has been quite good on events in North America 150 years ago, and as this diary notes, he has been superb on the gun nuts in this country.
           </p>
           <p>
            Pearce is a MUST read.
           </p>
           <p>
            Trolls, by the way, are quickly silenced there.
           </p>
           <p>
            If you are not reading Pearce, you are missing out on the obvious successor to irreplaceable Molly Ivins.
           </p>

                  <a href="/user/uid:32268">

                  </a>
                 </dd>
                </dl>
               </div>
               <div class="ct">
                <p>
                 There has been a sea change in attitude here as concerns standing up to the fanatics, and I welcome it with vigor. One can only spout bullshit for just so long before it will get called out.
                </p>
                <p>
                 There were some really nasty folks in that group, and some outrageous conduct in the swarming that they used to employ against those who spoke out. ranger995 and I - and others - had experiences which they couldn't match, so we were spared some of it, but others were treated brutally.
                </p>
                <p>
                 I care not where they went, but would find it rather amusing if they tried to come back and pick up where they left off - I think they would get their asses handed to them this time around.
                </p>
                <p>
                 There are still a few, but I don't think they will last long...
                </p>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               I stopped reading after I realized a huge logical error.
              </p>
              <p>
               I hope someone pointed it out. But it made me laugh.
              </p>
              <p>
               His intro (the Diary Ranger pointed out) was all about the right to bear arms and the (seemed to me quickly reading) to actually overthrow.
              </p>
              <p>
               Then he talks about why (Revolutionary war), and gets into how farmers, with little public support defeated the world's most powerful enemy.
              </p>
              <p>
               I don't know if his point was "look we don't need that many guns just a cause" or "look today we couldn't do that again."
              </p>
              <p>
               Either way I guess I thought it laughably disjointed because the only logical thing would be "we don't need that much" (as I doubt he'd be so foolish to point out hey these non gun-owning farmers overthrew the Brit Empire) so we need more guns when (well you get the point).
              </p>
              <p>
               But the converse brings up a more interesting point. If his numbers are right. That's like the risk of 20% of people being nuts and supporting, the tyranny of a radical minority.
              </p>
              <p>
               You know I don't want to even rationalize as Ranger pointed it out only because it was ludicrous but either way it's pretty laughable.
              </p>

               <div class="cx" id="cx53655288">
                <h5>
                 <a class="de">
                 </a>
                 <span class="cu">
                  That's not exactly what I meant
                 </span>
                 <span class="crd ntb">
                  (
                  <a href="/comments/1305673/53655288#c161?mode=alone;showrate=1#c161">
                   0+ / 0-
                  </a>
                  )
                 </span>
                </h5>
                <div class="ct">
                 <p>
                  I wanted to respond and was thinking as I typed.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I know people who are probably self pro-claimed gun owners who identify with conservatives because of an Anti-Gun Meme.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I disagree though with you we do need a different look. And we should care about the consensual characterization of the Democratic Platform. I am sure there are plenty non-crazy gun owners who agree (as the super majority of Americans do with stricter gun laws). When they see "D" next to a candidate they now associate it with taking everything away. Not gun sanity.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I think it extremely important that behind the dialogue that does not change the image of those speaking do for us. We are now dismissed (untruthfully) as non-gun owning, don't understand, etc.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  To take it to an extreme imagine minus the rhetoric you took issue with. 100 decorated veterans came back, progressives and said let's talk about the truth.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  My record does as well. But we have a fundamental public perception problem now that is anti-military despite who cut the GI Bill etc, and NO guns. If we shed the image of being at one end of a gun debate, there are many more we could reach who are sensible.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  As it is they have the choice between two viewpoints that although untrue are unpalatable. The NRA who at least is not invading. And what they THINK the D's stand for inaccurately we're taking your guns and ammo. Sure maybe eventually much un-needed incrementally. But I do not see how one could argue that who is the face of the Sane Gun Wing of the Party is matters and how vocal. As of now I am sure most think the party platform is take all away. And most think the military is against.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  Experts on guns, being vocally progressive simply resonates. This an issue to volatile too much money, put into framing us as an extreme. WHO WE HAVE matters and understanding the mentality to get through to the moderate gun owner matters. I thoroughly disagree.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  Who would someone who just gets an inkling voting D is against their social interests listen to: Joe the Plumber or a decorated and outspoken Colonel? The more gun experts the better. The more people saying I am a gun owner too, but, the better for the party.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  They have done too good of a job allowing us to look very distant, meek, anti-gun, to get the ear of someone who agrees with control for the most part. I think sad but true. Sometimes you do not change the message but how presented. And presented by people like this HELPS defuse the disinformation of Democrats.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  The man seems poised to be a Voice devoted to a goal we all agree. He is an asset. The more guns are not a politicized issue the better. Ie he's a D must be a City boy who never fired a pistol for fun.
                 </p>

           <p>
            Not that I don't endorse the sentiments, but I do think there are people in the Tea Party and Open Carry movements stupid enough to pick up the mocking challenge the Lt Col had laid down for them to "come and get me."
           </p>
           <p>
            These are people profoundly out of touch with reality. They're dumb schmucks who think that shooting some poor cop in the back of the head when he's trying to get a soda is an act of heroism.
           </p>
           <p>
            So there's no need to throw the gauntlet down. These jerks are itching to draw blood already, because that's what they think will make them a man. Yes, they're really that pathetic, but they are right on the cusp of becoming domestic terrorists. Some of them are over the line already.
           </p>
           <p>
            Standing up to people these demented people is brave enough, and it must be done; so in that I applaud Lt. Col Bateman. But Inviting them to have a go at you only turns what is a serious possibility into a probability.
           </p>
           <p>
            Maybe we need that. I can see that point of view. If the LV shootings aren't enough to put a stake in the heart of this particular madness, maybe we need a wave of domestic terrorism to come to our senses.  But I wouldn't invite anyone to take the opening shot in that wave, because what follows will be misfortune for innocent bystanders.

               <a href="/user/uid:976721">
                bearsguy
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              What is all this peer crap? It only breeds bullies and tyrants; One should be able to think on their own but I see with the baggers they have incorporated most of the non-thinkers. The poor little babies have lost, if they ever had, the ability of independent thought and so must rely on other minds for impetus.
             </p>
             <p>
              A clique that deprives one of using their minds is no place to be proud of. Yes, there is the camaraderie, and that has its uses if one is feeling alone in this world, but is not a replacement for independent thought and imagination.
              <br/>
             </p>

          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:989413">
             Joseph2222
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1305673/53651738#c155">
             Wed Jun 11, 2014 at 10:39:44 AM PDT
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <li id="c160">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53654411">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Problems from both sides.
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1305673/53654411#c160?mode=alone;showrate=1#c160">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            The problem, as I see it, on the left is that, while I understand the desire to keep the public safe, the politicians tend to (attempt to) go too far. They start to speak about confiscation of personal property from EVERYONE that owns a particular type of firearm ("assault weapons"). Confiscation by the government is just legalized theft.
            <br/>
            The way I see the problem on the right, is that they are defending an object that has been demonized, rightly or wrongly, for a couple decades. So the public sees them as endorsing murder. Another problem being the wingnuts that do things like the LV murders or the "open carry" at Chipotle.
            <br/>
            The really interesting part (when viewed as objectively as a human can be) is the largely emotional response from both sides. The left tends to argue guns being "evil" while the right espouses the 2nd Amendment and they are both dead set on their position being "in the right".
            <br/>
            Regardless of your position, intellectually we all must admit that guns themselves are not evil, they do not commit these atrocities alone. It's the people that are evil that are going out and killing. Do guns make that easier? Perhaps. Would more restrictions on ownership reduce the violence? Again, perhaps.
            <br/>
            The hard part being, how do you filter out the dangerous nutjobs from the people that just want to own a particular type of firearm? And if you could successfully determine who these nutjobs are, what do you do with them once they're identified? They're still dangerous with or without the gun. Do you take away their kitchen knives, bats, pipe, cars, and anything else that could be used to kill? Do you institutionalize them? How would we pay for that?
            <br/>
            I like the idea of pushing the mental health angle to reducing violence, it's likely going to be more effective than trying to reduce the number of guns already in private hands.
            <br/>
            As for the guys I hear talking about the vets that are willing to help "support and defend the constitution", the Bill of Rights is part of that, and the 2nd Amendment is part of that. That "well regulated militia" is made up of the people, therefore, the 2A states "the right of the people to keep and bear arms shall not be infringed". It doesn't say the right of the people in the militia, just "the people".
            <br/>
            Again, I don't think this is an argument that can be won, simply because intellectual dialogue won't likely change a person's deeply held beliefs on either side of the argument.
            <br/>
            If you haven't figured it out, I'm a gun owner, vet, 2A supporter, oathkeeper before it had a name, Constitutionalist, and typically polite and openminded. But I have my sticking points as well, and the 2nd Amendment is probably my worst one. But if you're polite to me I'll return in kind.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
